{\n\t\t\td.PendingPlugins = sets.New[string]()\n\t\t}\n\t\td.PendingPlugins.Insert(sts.Plugin())\n\t}\n}\n\n// Error returns detailed information of why the pod failed to fit on each node.\n// A message format is \"0/X nodes are available: <PreFilterMsg>. <FilterMsg>. <PostFilterMsg>.\"\nfunc (f *FitError) Error() string {\n\treasonMsg := fmt.Sprintf(NoNodeAvailableMsg+\":\", f.NumAllNodes)\n\tpreFilterMsg := f.Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg\n\tif preFilterMsg != \"\" {\n\t\t// PreFilter plugin returns unschedulable.\n\t\t// Add the messages from PreFilter plugins to reasonMsg.\n\t\treasonMsg += fmt.Sprintf(\" %v.\", preFilterMsg)\n\t}\n\n\tif preFilterMsg == \"\" {\n\t\t// the scheduling cycle went through PreFilter extension point successfully.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// When the prefilter plugin returns unschedulable,\n\t\t// the scheduling framework inserts the same unschedulable status to all nodes in NodeToStatusMap.\n\t\t// So, we shouldn't add the message from NodeToStatusMap when the PreFilter failed.\n\t\t// Otherwise, we will have duplicated reasons in the error message.\n\t\treasons := make(map[string]int)\n\t\tfor _, status := range f.Diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap {\n\t\t\tfor _, reason := range status.Reasons() {\n\t\t\t\treasons[reason]++\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tsortReasonsHistogram := func() []string {\n\t\t\tvar reasonStrings []string\n\t\t\tfor k, v := range reasons {\n\t\t\t\treasonStrings = append(reasonStrings, fmt.Sprintf(\"%v %v\", v, k))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tsort.Strings(reasonStrings)\n\t\t\treturn reasonStrings\n\t\t}\n\t\tsortedFilterMsg := sortReasonsHistogram()\n\t\tif len(sortedFilterMsg) != 0 {\n\t\t\treasonMsg += fmt.Sprintf(\" %v.\", strings.Join(sortedFilterMsg, \", \"))\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Add the messages from PostFilter plugins to reasonMsg.\n\t// We can add this message regardless of whether the scheduling cycle fails at PreFilter or Filter\n\t// since we may run PostFilter (if enabled) in both cases.\n\tpostFilterMsg := f.Diagnosis.PostFilterMsg\n\tif postFilterMsg != \"\" {\n\t\treasonMsg += fmt.Sprintf(\" %v\", postFilterMsg)\n\t}\n\treturn reasonMsg\n}\n\nfunc newAffinityTerm(pod *v1.Pod, term *v1.PodAffinityTerm) (*AffinityTerm, error) {\n\tselector, err := metav1.LabelSelectorAsSelector(term.LabelSelector)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tnamespaces := getNamespacesFromPodAffinityTerm(pod, term)\n\tnsSelector, err := metav1.LabelSelectorAsSelector(term.NamespaceSelector)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn &AffinityTerm{Namespaces: namespaces, Selector: selector, TopologyKey: term.TopologyKey, NamespaceSelector: nsSelector}, nil\n}\n\n// getAffinityTerms receives a Pod and affinity terms and returns the namespaces and\n// selectors of the terms.\nfunc getAffinityTerms(pod *v1.Pod, v1Terms []v1.PodAffinityTerm) ([]AffinityTerm, error) {\n\tif v1Terms == nil {\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t}\n\n\tvar terms []AffinityTerm\n\tfor i := range v1Terms {\n\t\tt, err := newAffinityTerm(pod, &v1Terms[i])\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t// We get here if the label selector failed to process\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tterms = append(terms, *t)\n\t}\n\treturn terms, nil\n}\n\n// getWeightedAffinityTerms returns the list of processed affinity terms.\nfunc getWeightedAffinityTerms(pod *v1.Pod, v1Terms []v1.WeightedPodAffinityTerm) ([]WeightedAffinityTerm, error) {\n\tif v1Terms == nil {\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t}\n\n\tvar terms []WeightedAffinityTerm\n\tfor i := range v1Terms {\n\t\tt, err := newAffinityTerm(pod, &v1Terms[i].PodAffinityTerm)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t// We get here if the label selector failed to process\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tterms = append(terms, WeightedAffinityTerm{AffinityTerm: *t, Weight: v1Terms[i].Weight})\n\t}\n\treturn terms, nil\n}\n\n// NewPodInfo returns a new PodInfo.\nfunc NewPodInfo(pod *v1.Pod) (*PodInfo, error) {\n\tpInfo := &PodInfo{}\n\terr := pInfo.Update(pod)\n\treturn pInfo, err\n}\n\nfunc getPodAffinityTerms(affinity *v1.Affinity) (terms []v1.PodAffinityTerm) {\n\tif affinity != nil && affinity.PodAffinity != nil {\n\t\tif len(affinity.PodAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution) != 0 {\n\t\t\tterms = affinity.PodAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution\n\t\t}\n\t\t// TODO: Uncomment this block when implement RequiredDuringSchedulingRequiredDuringExecution.\n\t\t// if len(affinity.PodAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingRequiredDuringExecution) != 0 {\n\t\t//\tterms = append(terms, affinity.PodAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingRequiredDuringExecution...)\n\t\t// }\n\t}\n\treturn terms\n}\n\nfunc getPodAntiAffinityTerms(affinity *v1.Affinity) (terms []v1.PodAffinityTerm) {\n\tif affinity != nil && affinity.PodAntiAffinity != nil {\n\t\tif len(affinity.PodAntiAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution) != 0 {\n\t\t\tterms = affinity.PodAntiAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution\n\t\t}\n\t\t// TODO: Uncomment this block when implement RequiredDuringSchedulingRequiredDuringExecution.\n\t\t// if len(affinity.PodAntiAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingRequiredDuringExecution) != 0 {\n\t\t//\tterms = append(terms, affinity.PodAntiAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingRequiredDuringExecution...)\n\t\t// }\n\t}\n\treturn terms\n}\n\n// returns a set of names according to the namespaces indicated in podAffinityTerm.\n// If namespaces is empty it considers the given pod's namespace.\nfunc getNamespacesFromPodAffinityTerm(pod *v1.Pod, podAffinityTerm *v1.PodAffinityTerm) sets.Set[string] {\n\tnames := sets.Set[string]{}\n\tif len(podAffinityTerm.Namespaces) == 0 && podAffinityTerm.NamespaceSelector == nil {\n\t\tnames.Insert(pod.Namespace)\n\t} else {\n\t\tnames.Insert(podAffinityTerm.Namespaces...)\n\t}\n\treturn names\n}\n\n// ImageStateSummary provides summarized information about the state of an image.\ntype ImageStateSummary struct {\n\t// Size of the image\n\tSize int64\n\t// Used to track how many nodes have this image, it is computed from the Nodes field below\n\t// during the execution of Snapshot.\n\tNumNodes int\n\t// A set of node names for nodes having this image present. This field is used for\n\t// keeping track of the nodes during update/add/remove events.\n\tNodes sets.Set[string]\n}\n\n// Snapshot returns a copy without Nodes field of ImageStateSummary\nfunc (iss *ImageStateSummary) Snapshot() *ImageStateSummary {\n\treturn &ImageStateSummary{\n\t\tSize:     iss.Size,\n\t\tNumNodes: iss.Nodes.Len(),\n\t}\n}\n\n// NodeInfo is node level aggregated information.\ntype NodeInfo struct {\n\t// Overall node information.\n\tnode *v1.Node\n\n\t// Pods running on the node.\n\tPods []*PodInfo\n\n\t// The subset of pods with affinity.\n\tPodsWithAffinity []*PodInfo\n\n\t// The subset of pods with required anti-affinity.\n\tPodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity []*PodInfo\n\n\t// Ports allocated on the node.\n\tUsedPorts HostPortInfo\n\n\t// Total requested resources of all pods on this node. This includes assumed\n\t// pods, which scheduler has sent for binding, but may not be scheduled yet.\n\tRequested *Resource\n\t// Total requested resources of all pods on this node with a minimum value\n\t// applied to each container's CPU and memory requests. This does not reflect\n\t// the actual resource requests for this node, but is used to avoid scheduling\n\t// many zero-request pods onto one node.\n\tNonZeroRequested *Resource\n\t// We store allocatedResources (which is Node.Status.Allocatable.*) explicitly\n\t// as int64, to avoid conversions and accessing map.\n\tAllocatable *Resource\n\n\t// ImageStates holds the entry of an image if and only if this image is on the node. The entry can be used for\n\t// checking an image's existence and advanced usage (e.g., image locality scheduling policy) based on the image\n\t// state information.\n\tImageStates map[string]*ImageStateSummary\n\n\t// PVCRefCounts contains a mapping of PVC names to the number of pods on the node using it.\n\t// Keys are in the format \"namespace/name\".\n\tPVCRefCounts map[string]int\n\n\t// Whenever NodeInfo changes, generation is bumped.\n\t// This is used to avoid cloning it if the object didn't change.\n\tGeneration int64\n}\n\n// nextGeneration: Let's make sure history never forgets the name...\n// Increments the generation number monotonically ensuring that generation numbers never collide.\n// Collision of the generation numbers would be particularly problematic if a node was deleted and\n// added back with the same name. See issue#63262.\nfunc nextGeneration() int64 {\n\treturn atomic.AddInt64(&generation, 1)\n}\n\n// Resource is a collection of compute resource.\ntype Resource struct {\n\tMilliCPU         int64\n\tMemory           int64\n\tEphemeralStorage int64\n\t// We store allowedPodNumber (which is Node.Status.Allocatable.Pods().Value())\n\t// explicitly as int, to avoid conversions and improve performance.\n\tAllowedPodNumber int\n\t// ScalarResources\n\tScalarResources map[v1.ResourceName]int64\n}\n\n// NewResource creates a Resource from ResourceList\nfunc NewResource(rl v1.ResourceList) *Resource {\n\tr := &Resource{}\n\tr.Add(rl)\n\treturn r\n}\n\n// Add adds ResourceList into Resource.\nfunc (r *Resource) Add(rl v1.ResourceList) {\n\tif r == nil {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tfor rName, rQuant := range rl {\n\t\tswitch rName {\n\t\tcase v1.ResourceCPU:\n\t\t\tr.MilliCPU += rQuant.MilliValue()\n\t\tcase v1.ResourceMemory:\n\t\t\tr.Memory += rQuant.Value()\n\t\tcase v1.ResourcePods:\n\t\t\tr.AllowedPodNumber += int(rQuant.Value())\n\t\tcase v1.ResourceEphemeralStorage:\n\t\t\tr.EphemeralStorage += rQuant.Value()\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tif schedutil.IsScalarResourceName(rName) {\n\t\t\t\tr.AddScalar(rName, rQuant.Value())\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// Clone returns a copy of this resource.\nfunc (r *Resource) Clone() *Resource {\n\tres := &Resource{\n\t\tMilliCPU:         r.MilliCPU,\n\t\tMemory:           r.Memory,\n\t\tAllowedPodNumber: r.AllowedPodNumber,\n\t\tEphemeralStorage: r.EphemeralStorage,\n\t}\n\tif r.ScalarResources != nil {\n\t\tres.ScalarResources = make(map[v1.ResourceName]int64, len(r.ScalarResources))\n\t\tfor k, v := range r.ScalarResources {\n\t\t\tres.ScalarResources[k] = v\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn res\n}\n\n// AddScalar adds a resource by a scalar value of this resource.\nfunc (r *Resource) AddScalar(name v1.ResourceName, quantity int64) {\n\tr.SetScalar(name, r.ScalarResources[name]+quantity)\n}\n\n// SetScalar sets a resource by a scalar value of this resource.\nfunc (r *Resource) SetScalar(name v1.ResourceName, quantity int64) {\n\t// Lazily allocate scalar resource map.\n\tif r.ScalarResources == nil {\n\t\tr.ScalarResources = map[v1.ResourceName]int64{}\n\t}\n\tr.ScalarResources[name] = quantity\n}\n\n// SetMaxResource compares with ResourceList and takes max value for each Resource.\nfunc (r *Resource) SetMaxResource(rl v1.ResourceList) {\n\tif r == nil {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tfor rName, rQuantity := range rl {\n\t\tswitch rName {\n\t\tcase v1.ResourceMemory:\n\t\t\tr.Memory = max(r.Memory, rQuantity.Value())\n\t\tcase v1.ResourceCPU:\n\t\t\tr.MilliCPU = max(r.MilliCPU, rQuantity.MilliValue())\n\t\tcase v1.ResourceEphemeralStorage:\n\t\t\tr.EphemeralStorage = max(r.EphemeralStorage, rQuantity.Value())\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tif schedutil.IsScalarResourceName(rName) {\n\t\t\t\tr.SetScalar(rName, max(r.ScalarResources[rName], rQuantity.Value()))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// NewNodeInfo returns a ready to use empty NodeInfo object.\n// If any pods are given in arguments, their information will be aggregated in\n// the returned object.\nfunc NewNodeInfo(pods ...*v1.Pod) *NodeInfo {\n\tni := &NodeInfo{\n\t\tRequested:        &Resource{},\n\t\tNonZeroRequested: &Resource{},\n\t\tAllocatable:      &Resource{},\n\t\tGeneration:       nextGeneration(),\n\t\tUsedPorts:        make(HostPortInfo),\n\t\tImageStates:      make(map[string]*ImageStateSummary),\n\t\tPVCRefCounts:     make(map[string]int),\n\t}\n\tfor _, pod := range pods {\n\t\tni.AddPod(pod)\n\t}\n\treturn ni\n}\n\n// Node returns overall information about this node.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) Node() *v1.Node {\n\tif n == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\treturn n.node\n}\n\n// Snapshot returns a copy of this node, Except that ImageStates is copied without the Nodes field.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) Snapshot() *NodeInfo {\n\tclone := &NodeInfo{\n\t\tnode:             n.node,\n\t\tRequested:        n.Requested.Clone(),\n\t\tNonZeroRequested: n.NonZeroRequested.Clone(),\n\t\tAllocatable:      n.Allocatable.Clone(),\n\t\tUsedPorts:        make(HostPortInfo),\n\t\tImageStates:      make(map[string]*ImageStateSummary),\n\t\tPVCRefCounts:     make(map[string]int),\n\t\tGeneration:       n.Generation,\n\t}\n\tif len(n.Pods) > 0 {\n\t\tclone.Pods = append([]*PodInfo(nil), n.Pods...)\n\t}\n\tif len(n.UsedPorts) > 0 {\n\t\t// HostPortInfo is a map-in-map struct\n\t\t// make sure it's deep copied\n\t\tfor ip, portMap := range n.UsedPorts {\n\t\t\tclone.UsedPorts[ip] = make(map[ProtocolPort]struct{})\n\t\t\tfor protocolPort, v := range portMap {\n\t\t\t\tclone.UsedPorts[ip][protocolPort] = v\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif len(n.PodsWithAffinity) > 0 {\n\t\tclone.PodsWithAffinity = append([]*PodInfo(nil), n.PodsWithAffinity...)\n\t}\n\tif len(n.PodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity) > 0 {\n\t\tclone.PodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity = append([]*PodInfo(nil), n.PodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity...)\n\t}\n\tif len(n.ImageStates) > 0 {\n\t\tstate := make(map[string]*ImageStateSummary, len(n.ImageStates))\n\t\tfor imageName, imageState := range n.ImageStates {\n\t\t\tstate[imageName] = imageState.Snapshot()\n\t\t}\n\t\tclone.ImageStates = state\n\t}\n\tfor key, value := range n.PVCRefCounts {\n\t\tclone.PVCRefCounts[key] = value\n\t}\n\treturn clone\n}\n\n// String returns representation of human readable format of this NodeInfo.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) String() string {\n\tpodKeys := make([]string, len(n.Pods))\n\tfor i, p := range n.Pods {\n\t\tpodKeys[i] = p.Pod.Name\n\t}\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"&NodeInfo{Pods:%v, RequestedResource:%#v, NonZeroRequest: %#v, UsedPort: %#v, AllocatableResource:%#v}\",\n\t\tpodKeys, n.Requested, n.NonZeroRequested, n.UsedPorts, n.Allocatable)\n}\n\n// AddPodInfo adds pod information to this NodeInfo.\n// Consider using this instead of AddPod if a PodInfo is already computed.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) AddPodInfo(podInfo *PodInfo) {\n\tn.Pods = append(n.Pods, podInfo)\n\tif podWithAffinity(podInfo.Pod) {\n\t\tn.PodsWithAffinity = append(n.PodsWithAffinity, podInfo)\n\t}\n\tif podWithRequiredAntiAffinity(podInfo.Pod) {\n\t\tn.PodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity = append(n.PodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity, podInfo)\n\t}\n\tn.update(podInfo.Pod, 1)\n}\n\n// AddPod is a wrapper around AddPodInfo.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) AddPod(pod *v1.Pod) {\n\t// ignore this err since apiserver doesn't properly validate affinity terms\n\t// and we can't fix the validation for backwards compatibility.\n\tpodInfo, _ := NewPodInfo(pod)\n\tn.AddPodInfo(podInfo)\n}\n\nfunc podWithAffinity(p *v1.Pod) bool {\n\taffinity := p.Spec.Affinity\n\treturn affinity != nil && (affinity.PodAffinity != nil || affinity.PodAntiAffinity != nil)\n}\n\nfunc podWithRequiredAntiAffinity(p *v1.Pod) bool {\n\taffinity := p.Spec.Affinity\n\treturn affinity != nil && affinity.PodAntiAffinity != nil &&\n\t\tlen(affinity.PodAntiAffinity.RequiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution) != 0\n}\n\nfunc removeFromSlice(logger klog.Logger, s []*PodInfo, k string) ([]*PodInfo, bool) {\n\tvar removed bool\n\tfor i := range s {\n\t\ttmpKey, err := GetPodKey(s[i].Pod)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Cannot get pod key\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(s[i].Pod))\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tif k == tmpKey {\n\t\t\t// delete the element\n\t\t\ts[i] = s[len(s)-1]\n\t\t\ts = s[:len(s)-1]\n\t\t\tremoved = true\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// resets the slices to nil so that we can do DeepEqual in unit tests.\n\tif len(s) == 0 {\n\t\treturn nil, removed\n\t}\n\treturn s, removed\n}\n\n// RemovePod subtracts pod information from this NodeInfo.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) RemovePod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error {\n\tk, err := GetPodKey(pod)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tif podWithAffinity(pod) {\n\t\tn.PodsWithAffinity, _ = removeFromSlice(logger, n.PodsWithAffinity, k)\n\t}\n\tif podWithRequiredAntiAffinity(pod) {\n\t\tn.PodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity, _ = removeFromSlice(logger, n.PodsWithRequiredAntiAffinity, k)\n\t}\n\n\tvar removed bool\n\tif n.Pods, removed = removeFromSlice(logger, n.Pods, k); removed {\n\t\tn.update(pod, -1)\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"no corresponding pod %s in pods of node %s\", pod.Name, n.node.Name)\n}\n\n// update node info based on the pod and sign.\n// The sign will be set to `+1` when AddPod and to `-1` when RemovePod.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) update(pod *v1.Pod, sign int64) {\n\tres, non0CPU, non0Mem := calculateResource(pod)\n\tn.Requested.MilliCPU += sign * res.MilliCPU\n\tn.Requested.Memory += sign * res.Memory\n\tn.Requested.EphemeralStorage += sign * res.EphemeralStorage\n\tif n.Requested.ScalarResources == nil && len(res.ScalarResources) > 0 {\n\t\tn.Requested.ScalarResources = map[v1.ResourceName]int64{}\n\t}\n\tfor rName, rQuant := range res.ScalarResources {\n\t\tn.Requested.ScalarResources[rName] += sign * rQuant\n\t}\n\tn.NonZeroRequested.MilliCPU += sign * non0CPU\n\tn.NonZeroRequested.Memory += sign * non0Mem\n\n\t// Consume ports when pod added or release ports when pod removed.\n\tn.updateUsedPorts(pod, sign > 0)\n\tn.updatePVCRefCounts(pod, sign > 0)\n\n\tn.Generation = nextGeneration()\n}\n\nfunc calculateResource(pod *v1.Pod) (Resource, int64, int64) {\n\tvar non0InitCPU, non0InitMem int64\n\tvar non0CPU, non0Mem int64\n\trequests := resourcehelper.PodRequests(pod, resourcehelper.PodResourcesOptions{\n\t\tInPlacePodVerticalScalingEnabled: utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.InPlacePodVerticalScaling),\n\t\tContainerFn: func(requests v1.ResourceList, containerType podutil.ContainerType) {\n\t\t\tnon0CPUReq, non0MemReq := schedutil.GetNonzeroRequests(&requests)\n\t\t\tswitch containerType {\n\t\t\tcase podutil.Containers:\n\t\t\t\tnon0CPU += non0CPUReq\n\t\t\t\tnon0Mem += non0MemReq\n\t\t\tcase podutil.InitContainers:\n\t\t\t\tnon0InitCPU = max(non0InitCPU, non0CPUReq)\n\t\t\t\tnon0InitMem = max(non0InitMem, non0MemReq)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\n\tnon0CPU = max(non0CPU, non0InitCPU)\n\tnon0Mem = max(non0Mem, non0InitMem)\n\n\t// If Overhead is being utilized, add to the non-zero cpu/memory tracking for the pod. It has already been added\n\t// into ScalarResources since it is part of requests\n\tif pod.Spec.Overhead != nil {\n\t\tif _, found := pod.Spec.Overhead[v1.ResourceCPU]; found {\n\t\t\tnon0CPU += pod.Spec.Overhead.Cpu().MilliValue()\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif _, found := pod.Spec.Overhead[v1.ResourceMemory]; found {\n\t\t\tnon0Mem += pod.Spec.Overhead.Memory().Value()\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tvar res Resource\n\tres.Add(requests)\n\treturn res, non0CPU, non0Mem\n}\n\n// updateUsedPorts updates the UsedPorts of NodeInfo.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) updateUsedPorts(pod *v1.Pod, add bool) {\n\tfor _, container := range pod.Spec.Containers {\n\t\tfor _, podPort := range container.Ports {\n\t\t\tif add {\n\t\t\t\tn.UsedPorts.Add(podPort.HostIP, string(podPort.Protocol), podPort.HostPort)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tn.UsedPorts.Remove(podPort.HostIP, string(podPort.Protocol), podPort.HostPort)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// updatePVCRefCounts updates the PVCRefCounts of NodeInfo.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) updatePVCRefCounts(pod *v1.Pod, add bool) {\n\tfor _, v := range pod.Spec.Volumes {\n\t\tif v.PersistentVolumeClaim == nil {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tkey := GetNamespacedName(pod.Namespace, v.PersistentVolumeClaim.ClaimName)\n\t\tif add {\n\t\t\tn.PVCRefCounts[key] += 1\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tn.PVCRefCounts[key] -= 1\n\t\t\tif n.PVCRefCounts[key] <= 0 {\n\t\t\t\tdelete(n.PVCRefCounts, key)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// SetNode sets the overall node information.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) SetNode(node *v1.Node) {\n\tn.node = node\n\tn.Allocatable = NewResource(node.Status.Allocatable)\n\tn.Generation = nextGeneration()\n}\n\n// RemoveNode removes the node object, leaving all other tracking information.\nfunc (n *NodeInfo) RemoveNode() {\n\tn.node = nil\n\tn.Generation = nextGeneration()\n}\n\n// GetPodKey returns the string key of a pod.\nfunc GetPodKey(pod *v1.Pod) (string, error) {\n\tuid := string(pod.UID)\n\tif len(uid) == 0 {\n\t\treturn \"\", errors.New(\"cannot get cache key for pod with empty UID\")\n\t}\n\treturn uid, nil\n}\n\n// GetNamespacedName returns the string format of a namespaced resource name.\nfunc GetNamespacedName(namespace, name string) string {\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", namespace, name)\n}\n\n// DefaultBindAllHostIP defines the default ip address used to bind to all host.\nconst DefaultBindAllHostIP = \"0.0.0.0\"\n\n// ProtocolPort represents a protocol port pair, e.g. tcp:80.\ntype ProtocolPort struct {\n\tProtocol string\n\tPort     int32\n}\n\n// NewProtocolPort creates a ProtocolPort instance.\nfunc NewProtocolPort(protocol string, port int32) *ProtocolPort {\n\tpp := &ProtocolPort{\n\t\tProtocol: protocol,\n\t\tPort:     port,\n\t}\n\n\tif len(pp.Protocol) == 0 {\n\t\tpp.Protocol = string(v1.ProtocolTCP)\n\t}\n\n\treturn pp\n}\n\n// HostPortInfo stores mapping from ip to a set of ProtocolPort\ntype HostPortInfo map[string]map[ProtocolPort]struct{}\n\n// Add adds (ip, protocol, port) to HostPortInfo\nfunc (h HostPortInfo) Add(ip, protocol string, port int32) {\n\tif port <= 0 {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\th.sanitize(&ip, &protocol)\n\n\tpp := NewProtocolPort(protocol, port)\n\tif _, ok := h[ip]; !ok {\n\t\th[ip] = map[ProtocolPort]struct{}{\n\t\t\t*pp: {},\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\th[ip][*pp] = struct{}{}\n}\n\n// Remove removes (ip, protocol, port) from HostPortInfo\nfunc (h HostPortInfo) Remove(ip, protocol string, port int32) {\n\tif port <= 0 {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\th.sanitize(&ip, &protocol)\n\n\tpp := {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_012SyTbuy2KEcF7iRym5JzH5","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Aha! I found something important. Looking at the EventsToRegister() method in the dynamicresources plugin, I can see:\n\n1. ResourceClaimParameters - Add | Update\n2. ResourceClassParameters - Add | Update\n3. ResourceClaim - Add | Update\n4. PodSchedulingContext - Add | Update\n5. Node - Add | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint\n6. ResourceClass - Add | Update\n\n**But there is NO ResourceSlice event registered!**\n\nThis is the bug! The dynamicresources plugin is using a ResourceSliceLister (as we saw earlier), which means it needs ResourceSlice events to update when ResourceSlices are created or updated by the DRA driver. However:\n\n1. The dynamicresources plugin is NOT registering ResourceSlice events in its EventsToRegister()\n2. The scheduler's eventhandlers.go file does NOT have a case for ResourceSlice in the switch statement that registers event handlers for various GVKs\n3. The framework/types.go file does NOT define a ResourceSlice GVK constant\n\nThis is the root cause of the bug!\n\nWhen a pod requests DRA devices and is initially unschedulable (because no ResourceSlices exist), the dynamicresources plugin marks it as unschedulable. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01CVAEiYkkswuKiVoznai4jX","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01FzTwHnQZsaes5kfTP1i7ss","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kubernetes Scheduler: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point for pod scheduling; implements the scheduling cycle that invokes plugins\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Registers event handlers for cluster resource changes; handles Pod, Node, Storage, and DRA-related resources\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — Defines GVK (Group/Version/Kind) constants for all resources that trigger scheduling queue re-evaluation\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — DRA plugin that validates pod resource claims; uses ResourceSliceLister but does NOT register ResourceSlice events\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1alpha2/types.go` — Defines ResourceSlice API type; used by DRA drivers to advertise available resources\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/interface.go` — SharedInformerFactory provides ResourceSlices() method for accessing ResourceSlice informer\n\n## Dependency Chain\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()`\n   - Pod requesting DRA devices arrives at scheduler\n   - Plugin execution reaches dynamicresources plugin PreFilter phase\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:EventsToRegister()`\n   - Plugin declares which events should trigger pod re-evaluation\n   - RegisterResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, etc. events registered\n   - **BUT ResourceSlice events are NOT registered** (missing line)\n\n3. **Propagated to**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:unionedGVKs()`\n   - Collects all GVKs from all plugins' EventsToRegister()\n   - Builds gvkMap: `map[framework.GVK]framework.ActionType`\n   - ResourceSlice GVK never added because plugin didn't request it\n\n4. **Passed to**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:addAllEventHandlers()`\n   - Iterates through gvkMap to register informer event handlers\n   - For each GVK, adds handler to move unschedulable pods to active/backoff queue on events\n   - **No case for ResourceSlice in switch statement** (lines 396-542)\n\n5. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` lines 68-106\n   - **ResourceSlice GVK constant is NOT DEFINED**\n   - Means plugins cannot register ResourceSlice events structurally\n   - UnrollWildCardResource() (lines 177-193) also missing ResourceSlice\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()` (approximately line 1215-1240)\n\n**Line**: Missing code block (should exist but doesn't)\n\n**Explanation**:\nThe dynamicresources plugin has three critical issues:\n\n1. **Missing Event Registration**: The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method registers events for ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaimParameters, and ResourceClassParameters, but **does NOT include ResourceSlice** events. This is the direct cause of the bug.\n\n2. **ResourceSlice Not in Framework**: The `framework/types.go` file defines GVK constants for other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, PodSchedulingContext) but **ResourceSlice is missing**. This blocks the ability to register the event handler.\n\n3. **Event Handler Not Implemented**: The `eventhandlers.go` file has a case for PodSchedulingContext (line 448), ResourceClaim (line 457), ResourceClass (line 466), ResourceClaimParameters (line 475), and ResourceClassParameters (line 484), but **no case for ResourceSlice**. Even if a plugin tried to register the event, the scheduler wouldn't know how to attach the event handler to the ResourceSlice informer.\n\n**Why This Causes the Bug**:\n- When a pod requesting DRA devices is scheduled before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices, the dynamicresources plugin's Filter hook returns `Unschedulable` because `structuredParameters.go:newResourceModel()` cannot find any ResourceSlices to validate available resources\n- The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the assumption that a future event will trigger re-evaluation\n- Later, when the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, there is NO event handler listening to ResourceSlice changes\n- No ClusterEvent is generated, so pods waiting in the unschedulable queue are never re-queued\n- **The pod remains stuck permanently in Unschedulable state**\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK to framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (after line 96)\n\nconst (\n\t// ... existing constants ...\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource() in framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (in UnrollWildCardResource function)\n\nfunc UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n\treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// ... existing events ...\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice event handler to eventhandlers.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go (in addAllEventHandlers function, after ResourceClassParameters case at line 492)\n\n\t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n### Fix 4: Add ResourceSlice events to dynamicresources plugin EventsToRegister() in dynamicresources.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go (in EventsToRegister method)\n\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n\tif !pl.enabled {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// ... existing events ...\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices published by DRA drivers may make pods schedulable by providing capacity information.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\nAnd add the corresponding QueueingHintFn:\n\n```diff\n// Add this method to the dynamicResources plugin struct\n\n+// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange is invoked for add and update resource slice events.\n+// It checks whether that change made a previously unschedulable pod schedulable.\n+// It errs on the side of letting a pod scheduling attempt happen.\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n+\t// Any ResourceSlice change might make a pod that uses structured parameters schedulable,\n+\t// so we should always retry.\n+\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (pod created before DRA driver starts):\n   - Pod with ResourceClaim arrives at scheduler\n   - `schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()` begins scheduling cycle\n   - Plugins execute PreFilter → Filter phases\n   - dynamicresources plugin's `Filter()` hook runs\n   - `structuredparameters.go:newResourceModel()` is called\n   - ResourceSliceLister has NO ResourceSlices (driver hasn't started)\n   - Plugin returns `Unschedulable` status: \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod marked as unschedulable, moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **Pod Queued for Re-evaluation** (scheduling cycle completes):\n   - Pod has UnschedulablePlugins = {dynamicResources}\n   - Stored in scheduler's unschedulable pod pool\n   - Waits for a registered ClusterEvent to trigger re-evaluation\n\n3. **DRA Driver Starts** (driver publishes ResourceSlice):\n   - DRA driver creates ResourceSlice objects with available resources\n   - ResourceSlice objects appear in apiserver\n   - **ResourceSlice informer receives Add event**\n   - **BUT no event handler is registered for ResourceSlice**\n   - Event is silently dropped (not delivered to scheduler)\n\n4. **Pod Stays Stuck** (race condition manifests):\n   - No ClusterEvent is generated for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Scheduler never calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue` for unschedulable pods\n   - Pod remains in unschedulable queue indefinitely\n   - Pod will never be retried unless another event (like Node change) happens\n\n### Why This is a Race Condition\n\n- **If driver starts FIRST**: ResourceSlices exist when pod arrives → dynamicresources plugin sees resources → scheduling succeeds\n- **If pod arrives FIRST**: No ResourceSlices exist → plugin marks pod unschedulable → driver starts and publishes ResourceSlices → but no event handler catches this → pod stuck forever\n\n### The Missing Link\n\nThe scheduler's event-driven architecture works like this:\n1. Plugins declare events they care about via `EventsToRegister()` → QueueingHintFn\n2. Scheduler registers event handlers for those events with informers\n3. When events fire, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with appropriate QueueingHints\n4. Unschedulable pods matching QueueingHints are retried\n\nResourceSlice events were never added to this pipeline, so they never trigger pod re-evaluation.\n\n## Impact\n\nThis bug prevents Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) from functioning in production scenarios where:\n- DRA drivers (like GPU device plugins) start after user pods\n- Pods request resources via ResourceClaim objects\n- Pods become permanently stuck if scheduling is attempted before driver publishes ResourceSlices\n\nThe fix ensures that whenever a DRA driver publishes or updates ResourceSlices, pods waiting for those resources are immediately re-evaluated for scheduling.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":413,"cache_read_input_tokens":70114,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":413},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c8601b26-a4b9-466a-ae14-ef2e5986b08f","uuid":"df3ac551-c902-4899-a963-a4de78d85f95"}

**ResourceSlice GVK constant is NOT DEFINED**\n   - Means plugins cannot register ResourceSlice events structurally\n   - UnrollWildCardResource() (lines 177-193) also missing ResourceSlice\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()` (approximately line 1215-1240)\n\n**Line**: Missing code block (should exist but doesn't)\n\n**Explanation**:\nThe dynamicresources plugin has three critical issues:\n\n1. **Missing Event Registration**: The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method registers events for ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaimParameters, and ResourceClassParameters, but **does NOT include ResourceSlice** events. This is the direct cause of the bug.\n\n2. **ResourceSlice Not in Framework**: The `framework/types.go` file defines GVK constants for other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, PodSchedulingContext) but **ResourceSlice is missing**. This blocks the ability to register the event handler.\n\n3. **Event Handler Not Implemented**: The `eventhandlers.go` file has a case for PodSchedulingContext (line 448), ResourceClaim (line 457), ResourceClass (line 466), ResourceClaimParameters (line 475), and ResourceClassParameters (line 484), but **no case for ResourceSlice**. Even if a plugin tried to register the event, the scheduler wouldn't know how to attach the event handler to the ResourceSlice informer.\n\n**Why This Causes the Bug**:\n- When a pod requesting DRA devices is scheduled before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices, the dynamicresources plugin's Filter hook returns `Unschedulable` because `structuredParameters.go:newResourceModel()` cannot find any ResourceSlices to validate available resources\n- The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the assumption that a future event will trigger re-evaluation\n- Later, when the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, there is NO event handler listening to ResourceSlice changes\n- No ClusterEvent is generated, so pods waiting in the unschedulable queue are never re-queued\n- **The pod remains stuck permanently in Unschedulable state**\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK to framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (after line \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource() in framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (in UnrollWildCardResource function)\n\nfunc UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n\treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// ... existing events ...\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice event handler to eventhandlers.go\n\n```diff\n// dynamicresources plugin EventsToRegister() in dynamicresources.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go (in EventsToRegister method)\n\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n\tif !pl.enabled {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// ... existing events ...\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices published by DRA drivers may make pods schedulable by pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\nAnd add the corresponding QueueingHintFn:\n\n```diff\n// Add this method to the dynamicResources plugin struct\n\n+// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange is invoked for add and update resource slice events.\n+// It checks whether that change made a previously unschedulable pod schedulable.\n+// It errs on the side of letting a pod scheduling attempt happen.\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n+\t// Any ResourceSlice change might make a pod that uses structured parameters schedulable,\n+\t// so we should always retry.\n+\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (pod created before DRA driver starts):\n   - Pod with ResourceClaim arrives at scheduler\n   - `schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()` begins scheduling cycle\n   - Plugins execute PreFilter → Filter phases\n   - dynamicresources plugin's `Filter()` hook runs\n   - `structuredparameters.go:newResourceModel()` is called\n   - ResourceSliceLister has NO ResourceSlices (driver hasn't started)\n   - Plugin returns `Unschedulable` status: \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod marked as unschedulable, moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **Pod Queued for Re-evaluation** (scheduling cycle completes):\n   - Pod has UnschedulablePlugins = {dynamicResources}\n   - Stored in scheduler's unschedulable pod pool\n   - Waits for a registered ClusterEvent to trigger re-evaluation\n\n3. **DRA Driver Starts** (driver publishes ResourceSlice):\n   - DRA driver creates ResourceSlice objects with available resources\n   - ResourceSlice objects appear in apiserver\n   - **ResourceSlice informer receives Add event**\n   - **BUT no event handler is registered for ResourceSlice**\n   - Event is silently dropped (not delivered to scheduler)\n\n4. **Pod Stays Stuck** (race condition manifests):\n   - No ClusterEvent is generated for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Scheduler never calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue` for unschedulable pods\n   - Pod remains in unschedulable queue indefinitely\n   - Pod will never be retried unless another event (like Node change) happens\n\n### Why This is a Race Condition\n\n- **If driver starts FIRST**: ResourceSlices exist when pod arrives → dynamicresources plugin sees resources → scheduling succeeds\n- **If pod arrives FIRST**: No ResourceSlices exist → plugin marks pod unschedulable → driver starts and publishes ResourceSlices → but no event handler catches this → pod stuck forever\n\n### The Missing Link\n\nThe scheduler's event-driven architecture works like this:\n1. Plugins declare events they care about via `EventsToRegister()` → QueueingHintFn\n2. Scheduler registers event handlers for those events with informers\n3. When events fire, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with appropriate QueueingHints\n4. Unschedulable pods matching QueueingHints are retried\n\nResourceSlice events were never added to this pipeline, so they never trigger pod re-evaluation.\n\n## Impact\n\nThis bug prevents Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) from functioning in production scenarios where:\n- DRA drivers (like GPU device plugins) start after user pods\n- Pods request resources via ResourceClaim objects\n- Pods become permanently stuck if scheduling is attempted before driver publishes ResourceSlices\n\nThe fix ensures that whenever a DRA driver publishes or updates ResourceSlices, pods waiting for those resources are immediately re-evaluated for scheduling.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Pod requesting DRA devices arrives at scheduler\n   - Plugin execution reaches dynamicresources plugin PreFilter phase\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:EventsToRegister()`\n   - Iterates through gvkMap to register informer event handlers\n   - For each GVK, adds handler to move unschedulable pods to active/backoff queue on events\n   - **No case for ResourceSlice in switch statement** (lines 396-542)\n\n5. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` lines 68-106\n   - This is the direct cause of the bug.\n\n2. **ResourceSlice Not in Framework**: The `framework/types.go` file defines GVK constants for other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, PodSchedulingContext) but **ResourceSlice is missing**. This blocks the ability to register the event handler.\n\n3. **Event Handler Not Implemented**: The `eventhandlers.go` file has a case for PodSchedulingContext (line 448), ResourceClaim (line 457), ResourceClass (line 466), ResourceClaimParameters (line 475), and ResourceClassParameters (line 484), but **no case for ResourceSlice**. Even if a plugin tried to register the event, the scheduler wouldn't know how to attach the event handler to the ResourceSlice informer.\n\n**Why This Causes the Bug**:\n- When a pod requesting DRA devices is scheduled before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices, the dynamicresources plugin's Filter hook returns `Unschedulable` because `structuredParameters.go:newResourceModel()` cannot find any ResourceSlices to validate available resources\n- The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the assumption that a future event will trigger re-evaluation\n- Later, when the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, there is NO event handler listening to ResourceSlice changes\n- No ClusterEvent is generated, so pods waiting in the unschedulable queue are never re-queued\n- **The Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (pod created before DRA driver starts):\n   - Pod with ResourceClaim arrives at scheduler\n   - `schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()` begins scheduling cycle\n   - Plugins execute PreFilter → Filter phases\n   - dynamicresources plugin's `Filter()` hook runs\n   - `structuredparameters.go:newResourceModel()` is called\n   - ResourceSliceLister has NO ResourceSlices (driver hasn't started)\n   - Plugin returns `Unschedulable` status: \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod marked as unschedulable, moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **Pod Queued for Re-evaluation** (scheduling cycle completes):\n   - Pod has UnschedulablePlugins = {dynamicResources}\n   - Stored in scheduler's unschedulable pod pool\n   - Waits for a registered ClusterEvent to trigger re-evaluation\n\n3. **DRA Driver Starts** (driver publishes ResourceSlice):\n   - DRA driver creates ResourceSlice objects with available resources\n   - ResourceSlice objects appear in apiserver\n   - **ResourceSlice informer receives Add event**\n   - **BUT no event handler is registered for ResourceSlice**\n   - Event is silently dropped (not delivered to scheduler)\n\n4. **Pod Stays Stuck** (race condition manifests):\n   - No ClusterEvent is generated for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Scheduler never calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue` for unschedulable pods\n   - Pod remains in unschedulable queue indefinitely\n   - Pod will never be retried unless another event (like Node change) happens\n\n### Why This is a Race Condition\n\n- **If driver starts FIRST**: ResourceSlices exist when pod arrives → dynamicresources plugin sees resources → scheduling succeeds\n- **If pod arrives FIRST**: No ResourceSlices exist → plugin marks pod unschedulable → driver starts and publishes ResourceSlices → but no event handler catches this → pod stuck forever\n\n### The Missing Link\n\nThe scheduler's event-driven architecture works like this:\n1. Plugins declare events they care about via `EventsToRegister()` → QueueingHintFn\n2. Scheduler registers event handlers for those events with informers\n3. When events fire, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with appropriate QueueingHints\n4. Unschedulable pods matching QueueingHints are retried\n\nResourceSlice events were never added to this pipeline, so they never trigger pod re-evaluation.\n\n## Impact\n\nThis bug prevents Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) from functioning in production scenarios where:\n- DRA drivers (like GPU device plugins) start after user pods\n- Pods request resources via ResourceClaim objects\n- Pods become permanently stuck if scheduling is attempted before driver publishes ResourceSlices\n\nThe fix ensures that whenever a DRA driver publishes or updates ResourceSlices, pods waiting for those resources are immediately re-evaluated for scheduling.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":37,"oldLines":9,"newStart":37,"newLines":9,"lines":[" "," **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`"," ","-**Function**: `EventsToRegister()` (approximately line 1215-1240)","+**Function**: `EventsToRegister()` (line 381-413)"," ","-**Line**: Missing code block (should exist but doesn't)","+**Line**: ~410-411 (missing code block after ResourceClass event)"," "," **Explanation**:"," The dynamicresources plugin has three critical issues:"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

— Entry point for pod scheduling; implements the scheduling cycle that invokes plugins\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Registers event handlers for cluster resource changes; handles Pod, Node, Storage, and DRA-related resources\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — Defines GVK (Group/Version/Kind) constants for all resources that trigger scheduling queue re-evaluation\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — DRA plugin that validates pod resource claims; uses ResourceSliceLister but does NOT register ResourceSlice events\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1alpha2/types.go` — Defines ResourceSlice API type; used by DRA drivers to advertise available resources\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/interface.go` — SharedInformerFactory provides ResourceSlices() method for accessing ResourceSlice informer\n\n## Dependency Chain\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()`\n   - Pod requesting DRA devices arrives at scheduler\n   - Plugin execution reaches dynamicresources plugin PreFilter phase\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:EventsToRegister()`\n   - Plugin declares which events should trigger pod re-evaluation\n   - RegisterResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, etc. events registered\n   - **BUT ResourceSlice events are NOT registered** (missing line)\n\n3. **Propagated to**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:unionedGVKs()`\n   - Collects all GVKs from all plugins' EventsToRegister()\n   - Builds gvkMap: `map[framework.GVK]framework.ActionType`\n   - ResourceSlice GVK never added because plugin didn't request it\n\n4. **Passed to**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:addAllEventHandlers()`\n   - Iterates through gvkMap to register informer event handlers\n   - For each GVK, adds handler to move unschedulable pods to active/backoff queue on events\n   - **No case for ResourceSlice in switch statement** (lines 396-542)\n\n5. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` lines 68-106\n   - **ResourceSlice GVK constant is NOT DEFINED**\n   - Means plugins cannot register ResourceSlice events structurally\n   - UnrollWildCardResource() (lines 177-193) also missing ResourceSlice\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()` (line 381-413)\n\n**Line**: ~410-411 (missing code block after ResourceClass event)\n\n**Explanation**:\nThe dynamicresources plugin has three critical issues:\n\n1. **Missing Event Registration**: The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method registers events for ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaimParameters, and ResourceClassParameters, but **does NOT include ResourceSlice** events. This is the direct cause of the bug.\n\n2. **ResourceSlice Not in Framework**: The `framework/types.go` file defines GVK constants for other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, PodSchedulingContext) but **ResourceSlice is missing**. This blocks the ability to register the event handler.\n\n3. **Event Handler Not Implemented**: The `eventhandlers.go` file has a case for PodSchedulingContext (line 448), ResourceClaim (line 457), ResourceClass (line 466), ResourceClaimParameters (line 475), and ResourceClassParameters (line 484), but **no case for ResourceSlice**. Even if a plugin tried to register the event, the scheduler wouldn't know how to attach the event handler to the ResourceSlice informer.\n\n**Why This Causes the Bug**:\n- When a pod requesting DRA devices is scheduled before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices, the dynamicresources plugin's Filter hook returns `Unschedulable` because `structuredParameters.go:newResourceModel()` cannot find any ResourceSlices to validate available resources\n- The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the assumption that a future event will trigger re-evaluation\n- Later, when the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, there is NO event handler listening to ResourceSlice changes\n- No ClusterEvent is generated, so pods waiting in the unschedulable queue are never re-queued\n- **The pod remains stuck permanently in Unschedulable state**\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK to framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (after line 96)\n\nconst (\n\t// ... existing constants ...\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource() in framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (in UnrollWildCardResource function)\n\nfunc UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n\treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// ... existing events ...\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice event handler to eventhandlers.go\n\n```diff\n// informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n### Fix 4: Add ResourceSlice events to pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\nAnd add the corresponding QueueingHintFn:\n\n```diff\n// Add this method to the dynamicResources plugin struct\n\n+// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange is invoked for add and update resource slice events.\n+// It checks whether that change made a previously unschedulable pod schedulable.\n+// It errs on the side of letting a pod scheduling attempt happen.\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n+\t// Any ResourceSlice change might make a pod that uses structured parameters schedulable,\n+\t// so we should always retry.\n+\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (pod created before DRA driver starts):\n   - Pod with ResourceClaim arrives at scheduler\n   - `schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()` begins scheduling cycle\n   - Plugins execute PreFilter → Filter phases\n   - dynamicresources plugin's `Filter()` hook runs\n   - `structuredparameters.go:newResourceModel()` is called\n   - ResourceSliceLister has NO ResourceSlices (driver hasn't started)\n   - Plugin returns `Unschedulable` status: \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod marked as unschedulable, moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **Pod Queued for Re-evaluation** (scheduling cycle completes):\n   - Pod has UnschedulablePlugins = {dynamicResources}\n   - Stored in scheduler's unschedulable pod pool\n   - Waits for a registered ClusterEvent to trigger re-evaluation\n\n3. **DRA Driver Starts** (driver publishes ResourceSlice):\n   - DRA driver creates ResourceSlice objects with available resources\n   - ResourceSlice objects appear in apiserver\n   - **ResourceSlice informer receives Add event**\n   - **BUT no event handler is registered for ResourceSlice**\n   - Event is silently dropped (not delivered to scheduler)\n\n4. **Pod Stays Stuck** (race condition manifests):\n   - No ClusterEvent is generated for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Scheduler never calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue` for unschedulable pods\n   - Pod remains in unschedulable queue indefinitely\n   - Pod will never be retried unless another event (like Node change) happens\n\n### Why This is a Race Condition\n\n- **If driver starts FIRST**: ResourceSlices exist when pod arrives → dynamicresources plugin sees resources → scheduling succeeds\n- **If pod arrives FIRST**: No ResourceSlices exist → plugin marks pod unschedulable → driver starts and publishes ResourceSlices → but no event handler catches this → pod stuck forever\n\n### The Missing Link\n\nThe scheduler's event-driven architecture works like this:\n1. Plugins declare events they care about via `EventsToRegister()` → QueueingHintFn\n2. Scheduler registers event handlers for those events with informers\n3. When events fire, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with appropriate QueueingHints\n4. Unschedulable pods matching QueueingHints are retried\n\nResourceSlice events were never added to this pipeline, so they never trigger pod re-evaluation.\n\n## Impact\n\nThis bug prevents Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) from functioning in production scenarios where:\n- DRA drivers (like GPU device plugins) start after user pods\n- Pods request resources via ResourceClaim objects\n- Pods become permanently stuck if scheduling is attempted before driver publishes ResourceSlices\n\nThe fix ensures that whenever a DRA driver publishes or updates ResourceSlices, pods waiting for those resources are immediately re-evaluated for scheduling.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":118,"oldLines":7,"newStart":118,"newLines":7,"lines":[" ### Fix 4: Add ResourceSlice events to dynamicresources Scheduler: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point for pod scheduling; implements the scheduling cycle that invokes plugins\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Registers event handlers for cluster resource changes; handles Pod, Node, Storage, and DRA-related resources\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — Defines GVK (Group/Version/Kind) constants for all resources that trigger scheduling queue re-evaluation\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — DRA plugin that validates pod resource claims; uses ResourceSliceLister but does NOT register ResourceSlice events\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1alpha2/types.go` — Defines ResourceSlice API type; used by DRA drivers to advertise available resources\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/interface.go` — SharedInformerFactory provides ResourceSlices() method for accessing ResourceSlice informer\n\n## Dependency Chain\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()`\n   - Pod requesting DRA devices arrives at scheduler\n   - Plugin execution reaches dynamicresources plugin PreFilter phase\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:EventsToRegister()`\n   - Plugin declares which events should trigger pod re-evaluation\n   - RegisterResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, etc. events registered\n   - **BUT ResourceSlice events are NOT registered** (missing line)\n\n3. **Propagated to**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:unionedGVKs()`\n   - Collects all GVKs from all plugins' EventsToRegister()\n   - Builds gvkMap: `map[framework.GVK]framework.ActionType`\n   - ResourceSlice GVK never added because plugin didn't request it\n\n4. **Passed to**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:addAllEventHandlers()`\n   - Iterates through gvkMap to register informer event handlers\n   - For each GVK, adds handler to move unschedulable pods to active/backoff queue on events\n   - **No case for ResourceSlice in switch statement** (lines 396-542)\n\n5. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` lines 68-106\n   - **ResourceSlice GVK constant is NOT DEFINED**\n   - Means plugins cannot register ResourceSlice events structurally\n   - UnrollWildCardResource() (lines 177-193) also missing ResourceSlice\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()` (line 381-413)\n\n**Line**: ~410-411 (missing code block after ResourceClass event)\n\n**Explanation**:\nThe dynamicresources plugin has three critical issues:\n\n1. **Missing Event Registration**: The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method registers events for ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaimParameters, and ResourceClassParameters, but **does NOT include ResourceSlice** events. This is the direct cause of the bug.\n\n2. **ResourceSlice Not in Framework**: The `framework/types.go` file defines GVK constants for other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, PodSchedulingContext) but **ResourceSlice is missing**. This blocks the ability to register the event handler.\n\n3. **Event Handler Not Implemented**: The `eventhandlers.go` file has a case for PodSchedulingContext (line 448), ResourceClaim (line 457), ResourceClass (line 466), ResourceClaimParameters (line 475), and ResourceClassParameters (line 484), but **no case for ResourceSlice**. Even if a plugin tried to register the event, the scheduler wouldn't know how to attach the event handler to the ResourceSlice informer.\n\n**Why This Causes the Bug**:\n- When a pod requesting DRA devices is scheduled before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices, the dynamicresources plugin's Filter hook returns `Unschedulable` because `structuredParameters.go:newResourceModel()` cannot find any ResourceSlices to validate available resources\n- The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the assumption that a future event will trigger re-evaluation\n- Later, when the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, there is NO event handler listening to ResourceSlice changes\n- No ClusterEvent is generated, so pods waiting in the unschedulable queue are never re-queued\n- **The pod remains stuck permanently in Unschedulable state**\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK to framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (after line 96)\n\nconst (\n\t// ... existing constants ...\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource() in framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (in UnrollWildCardResource function)\n\nfunc UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n\treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// ... existing events ...\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice event handler to eventhandlers.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go (in addAllEventHandlers function, after ResourceClassParameters case at line 492)\n\n\t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n### Fix 4: Add ResourceSlice events to dynamicresources plugin EventsToRegister() in dynamicresources.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go (lines 381-412)\n\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n\tif !pl.enabled {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// A note about UpdateNodeTaint event:\n\t\t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n\t\t// As a common problematic scenario,\n\t\t// when a node is added but not ready, NodeAdd event is filtered out by preCheck and doesn't arrive.\n\t\t// In such cases, this plugin may miss some events that actually make pods schedulable.\n\t\t// As a workaround, we add UpdateNodeTaint event to catch the case.\n\t\t// We can remove UpdateNodeTaint when we remove the preCheck feature.\n\t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n\t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices published by DRA drivers may make pods schedulable by providing capacity information.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\nAnd add the corresponding QueueingHintFn method after the other isSchedulableAfter* methods:\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go (after line 500 or similar)\n\n+// isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange is invoked for add and update resource slice events.\n+// It checks whether that change made a previously unschedulable pod schedulable.\n+// ResourceSlices are added by DRA drivers to advertise available resources, which may\n+// allow previously stuck pods to be allocated.\n+// It errs on the side of letting a pod scheduling attempt happen.\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (framework.QueueingHint, error) {\n+\t// Any ResourceSlice change might make a pod that uses structured parameters schedulable,\n+\t// so we should always retry scheduling for pods using claims.\n+\treturn framework.Queue, nil\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Execution Path from Symptom to Root Cause\n\n1. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (pod created before DRA driver starts):\n   - Pod with ResourceClaim arrives at scheduler\n   - `schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()` begins scheduling cycle\n   - Plugins execute PreFilter → Filter phases\n   - dynamicresources plugin's `Filter()` hook runs\n   - `structuredparameters.go:newResourceModel()` is called\n   - ResourceSliceLister has NO ResourceSlices (driver hasn't started)\n   - Plugin returns `Unschedulable` status: \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod marked as unschedulable, moved to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **Pod Queued for Re-evaluation** (scheduling cycle completes):\n   - Pod has UnschedulablePlugins = {dynamicResources}\n   - Stored in scheduler's unschedulable pod pool\n   - Waits for a registered ClusterEvent to trigger re-evaluation\n\n3. **DRA Driver Starts** (driver publishes ResourceSlice):\n   - DRA driver creates ResourceSlice objects with available resources\n   - ResourceSlice objects appear in apiserver\n   - **ResourceSlice informer receives Add event**\n   - **BUT no event handler is registered for ResourceSlice**\n   - Event is silently dropped (not delivered to scheduler)\n\n4. **Pod Stays Stuck** (race condition manifests):\n   - No ClusterEvent is generated for ResourceSlice changes\n   - Scheduler never calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue` for unschedulable pods\n   - Pod remains in unschedulable queue indefinitely\n   - Pod will never be retried unless another event (like Node change) happens\n\n### Why This is a Race Condition\n\n- **If driver starts FIRST**: ResourceSlices exist when pod arrives → dynamicresources plugin sees resources → scheduling succeeds\n- **If pod arrives FIRST**: No ResourceSlices exist → plugin marks pod unschedulable → driver starts and publishes ResourceSlices → but no event handler catches this → pod stuck forever\n\n### The Missing Link\n\nThe scheduler's event-driven architecture works like this:\n1. Plugins declare events they care about via `EventsToRegister()` → QueueingHintFn\n2. Scheduler registers event handlers for those events with informers\n3. When events fire, handlers call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with appropriate QueueingHints\n4. Unschedulable pods matching QueueingHints are retried\n\nResourceSlice events were never added to this pipeline, so they never trigger pod re-evaluation.\n\n## Impact\n\nThis bug prevents Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) from functioning in production scenarios where:\n- DRA drivers (like GPU device plugins) start after user pods\n- Pods request resources via ResourceClaim objects\n- Pods become permanently stuck if scheduling is attempted before driver publishes ResourceSlices\n\nThe fix ensures that whenever a DRA driver publishes or updates ResourceSlices, pods waiting for those resources are immediately re-evaluated for scheduling.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":62,"oldLines":7,"newStart":62,"newLines":7,"lines":[" ### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK to framework/types.go"," "," ```diff","-// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (after line 96)","+// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (lines 67-106)"," "," const (","   // ... existing constants ..."]},{"oldStart":72,"oldLines":16,"newStart":72,"newLines":34,"lines":[" +\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\""," ","   // WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.","+  // e.g., If you register `{Resource: \"*\", ActionType: All}` in EventsToRegister,","+  // all coming clusterEvents will be admitted. Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point for pod scheduling; implements the scheduling cycle that invokes plugins\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Registers event handlers for cluster resource changes; handles Pod, Node, Storage, and DRA-related resources\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — Defines GVK (Group/Version/Kind) constants for all resources that trigger scheduling queue re-evaluation\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — DRA plugin that validates pod resource claims; uses ResourceSliceLister but does NOT register ResourceSlice events\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1alpha2/types.go` — Defines ResourceSlice API type; used by DRA drivers to advertise available resources\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/interface.go` — SharedInformerFactory provides ResourceSlices() method for accessing ResourceSlice informer\n\n## Dependency Chain\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:ScheduleOne()`\n   - Pod requesting DRA devices arrives at scheduler\n   - Plugin execution reaches dynamicresources plugin PreFilter phase\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:EventsToRegister()`\n   - Plugin declares which events should trigger pod re-evaluation\n   - RegisterResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, etc. events registered\n   - **BUT ResourceSlice events are NOT registered** (missing line)\n\n3. **Propagated to**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:unionedGVKs()`\n   - Collects all GVKs from all plugins' EventsToRegister()\n   - Builds gvkMap: `map[framework.GVK]framework.ActionType`\n   - ResourceSlice GVK never added because plugin didn't request it\n\n4. **Passed to**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:addAllEventHandlers()`\n   - Iterates through gvkMap to register informer event handlers\n   - For each GVK, adds handler to move unschedulable pods to active/backoff queue on events\n   - **No case for ResourceSlice in switch statement** (lines 396-542)\n\n5. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` lines 68-106\n   - **ResourceSlice GVK constant is NOT DEFINED**\n   - Means plugins cannot register ResourceSlice events structurally\n   - UnrollWildCardResource() (lines 177-193) also missing ResourceSlice\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n**Function**: `EventsToRegister()` (line 381-413)\n\n**Line**: ~410-411 (missing code block after ResourceClass event)\n\n**Explanation**:\nThe dynamicresources plugin has three critical issues:\n\n1. **Missing Event Registration**: The plugin's `EventsToRegister()` method registers events for ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaimParameters, and ResourceClassParameters, but **does NOT include ResourceSlice** events. This is the direct cause of the bug.\n\n2. **ResourceSlice Not in Framework**: The `framework/types.go` file defines GVK constants for other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, PodSchedulingContext) but **ResourceSlice is missing**. This blocks the ability to register the event handler.\n\n3. **Event Handler Not Implemented**: The `eventhandlers.go` file has a case for PodSchedulingContext (line 448), ResourceClaim (line 457), ResourceClass (line 466), ResourceClaimParameters (line 475), and ResourceClassParameters (line 484), but **no case for ResourceSlice**. Even if a plugin tried to register the event, the scheduler wouldn't know how to attach the event handler to the ResourceSlice informer.\n\n**Why This Causes the Bug**:\n- When a pod requesting DRA devices is scheduled before the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlices, the dynamicresources plugin's Filter hook returns `Unschedulable` because `structuredParameters.go:newResourceModel()` cannot find any ResourceSlices to validate available resources\n- The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the assumption that a future event will trigger re-evaluation\n- Later, when the DRA driver publishes ResourceSlice objects, there is NO event handler listening to ResourceSlice changes\n- No ClusterEvent is generated, so pods waiting in the unschedulable queue are never re-queued\n- **The pod remains stuck permanently in Unschedulable state**\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK to framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (lines 67-106)\n\nconst (\n\t// ... existing constants ...\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n\t// e.g., If you register `{Resource: \"*\", ActionType: All}` in EventsToRegister,\n\t// all coming clusterEvents will be admitted. Be careful to register it, it will\n\t// increase the computing pressure in requeueing unless you really need it.\n\t//\n\t// Meanwhile, if the coming clusterEvent is a wildcard one, all pods\n\t// will be moved from unschedulablePod pool to activeQ/backoffQ forcibly.\n\tWildCard GVK = \"*\"\n)\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource() in framework/types.go\n\n```diff\n// pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go (lines 177-193)\n\nfunc UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n\treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType:
